<div id="review_2780134184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2780134184" />
    <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma"><img alt="PattyMacDotComma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577835191p2/1128612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2780134184?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PattyMacDotComma" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma">PattyMacDotComma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781492660637" href="/book/show/34431455-my-cousin-rachel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=aa">aa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=aa-col">aa-col</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=mystery-crime-thriller">mystery-crime-thriller</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2780134184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17103982855470702272"><b>4★<br/>“Ambrose had been so right when he used to say that women were a race apart.<br/>. . . <br/>This, I thought to myself, is another trick of women, to throw a Jest in the air that left a sting behind it.<br/>. . . <br/>That was the infuriating thing about a woman. Always the last word. Leaving one to grapple with ill-temper, and she herself serene. A woman, it seemed, was never in the wrong. Or if she was, she twisted the fault to her advantage, making it seem otherwise.”</b><br/><br/>Ambrose Ashley was the confirmed bachelor wh</span>
  <span id="freeText17103982855470702272" style="display:none"><b>4★<br />“Ambrose had been so right when he used to say that women were a race apart.<br />. . . <br />This, I thought to myself, is another trick of women, to throw a Jest in the air that left a sting behind it.<br />. . . <br />That was the infuriating thing about a woman. Always the last word. Leaving one to grapple with ill-temper, and she herself serene. A woman, it seemed, was never in the wrong. Or if she was, she twisted the fault to her advantage, making it seem otherwise.”</b><br /><br />Ambrose Ashley was the confirmed bachelor who raised his orphaned little cousin, Philip Ashley, on the family estate in Cornwall. They were clearly well-suited to each other, and Philip was raised enjoying their privileged status and their circle of friends. The estate collected rents from tenants and was a thriving business, with grounds running down to the sea. They give some cast-off clothing to the tenants (for Christmas!) – that kind of privilege.<br /><br /><b>“Ambrose at twenty-seven was god of all creation, certainly god of my own narrow world, and the whole object of my life was to resemble him.”</b><br /><br />As Ambrose got older, he had to head for warmer climes in the winter for his health, and Philip assumed some responsibility for the day-to-day management of the business, but of course, it was the staff who ran the household and his godfather who handled the finances. He was pretty much fancy-free.<br /><br /><b>“<i>‘And now sit back in your chairs and be comfortable, gentlemen. As there is no woman in the house we can put our boots on the table and spit on the carpet.’</i>”</b><br /><br />It’s all dogs and pipes and rambles and musings and missing Ambrose, until suddenly Ambrose writes that he has married a distant cousin, Rachel, and is not coming home this summer. Philip is jealous to the core, and when Ambrose dies of an undetermined illness, he is beside himself with suspicion and hatred.<br /><br />I think I must have seen the 1952 film, because I kept picturing Olivia de Havilland’s expression changing subtly from sorrow and regret to joy and delight, depending on the circumstances. But I had completely forgotten Richard Burton as young Philip, and even now, I find it difficult to imagine because he had such a powerful presence as an older man.<br /><br />Philip is not a country bumpkin. He was sent away to school and educated well. They often had dinner guests from among the other landowners and people of influence, but servants were servants, the working class was the working class, and he was pretty sheltered.<br /><br />We meet him when he’s 25, remembering his boyhood and the past year. He grew up to look uncannily like his older cousin. It’s not such a surprise that he would behave like Ambrose, as he clearly idolised him.<br /><br />I enjoyed this a lot and seeing how du Maurier deals with the light and shade of relationships. You can’t help wanting to shake and throttle young Philip from time to time, but that’s half the fun. <br /><br />Her descriptions of the landscape, weather, the dust in the old rooms, the clothing and the changing thereof (or not) set the scene perfectly. <br /><br /><b>“The shocks of corn were golden in the last rays of the sun. The sea was very blue, almost purple where it covered the rocks, and had that deep full look about it that always comes with the flood tide. The fishing fleet had put out, and were standing eastward to catch the shore breeze. Back at home the house was in shadow now, only the weathervane on the top of the clock tower catching a loose shaft of light.”</b><br /><br />I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17899948.Rebecca" title="Rebecca by Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebecca</a> better, it’s more suspenseful, but this is still a good story about a mysterious woman! And now, I’m going to watch the old film and see how well it stands up.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17103982855470702272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1858765753" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1858765753" />
    <a title="Iris P" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2641948-iris-p"><img alt="Iris P" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483406411p2/2641948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1858765753?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iris P" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iris P" href="/user/show/2641948-iris-p">Iris P</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19520435-my-cousin-rachel">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers who love mysteries novels, gothic novels</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2641948-iris-p?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2641948-iris-p?shelf=mysteries-thrillers">mysteries-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2641948-iris-p?shelf=overdrive-library">overdrive-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2641948-iris-p?shelf=gothic-theme">gothic-theme</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2641948-iris-p?shelf=british-lit">british-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1858765753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5494995730910752410"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18869970.My_Cousin_Rachel' title='My Cousin Rachel by Daphne du Maurier' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Cousin Rachel</a><br/><br/>★★★ 3 ½ Stars<br/><br/><br/>If you haven't read this novel yet here's a short synopsis from the book blurb:<br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Orphaned at an early age, Philip Ashley is raised by his benevolent older cousin, Ambrose. Resolutely single, Ambrose delights in Philip as his heir, a man who will love his grand home as much as he does himself. But the cozy world the two construct is shattered when Ambrose sets off on a trip to Florence. There he falls in love and marries - and there he dies suddenly.<br/>Jealous of h</blockquote></b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText5494995730910752410" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18869970.My_Cousin_Rachel" title="My Cousin Rachel by Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">My Cousin Rachel</a><br /><br />★★★ 3 ½ Stars<br /><br /><br />If you haven't read this novel yet here's a short synopsis from the book blurb:<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Orphaned at an early age, Philip Ashley is raised by his benevolent older cousin, Ambrose. Resolutely single, Ambrose delights in Philip as his heir, a man who will love his grand home as much as he does himself. But the cozy world the two construct is shattered when Ambrose sets off on a trip to Florence. There he falls in love and marries - and there he dies suddenly.<br />Jealous of his marriage, racked by suspicion at the hints in Ambrose's letters, and grief-stricken by his death, Philip prepares to meet his cousin's widow with hatred in his heart.<br />Despite himself, Philip is drawn to this beautiful, sophisticated, mysterious Rachel like a moth to the flame. And yet . . . might she have had a hand in Ambrose's death?</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />***********************************************<br /><br />I suppose it is only inevitable that, once you read your first novel by an author, you find yourself comparing the subsequent ones to that first experience and, even subconsciously, hoping to replicate it. In this case, my reaction might be heightened by the fact that the one novel I'd read by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2001717.Daphne_du_Maurier" title="Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daphne du Maurier</a> was probably her <i>magnum opus</i>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17899948.Rebecca" title="Rebecca by Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebecca</a>. <br /><br />I certainly enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18869970.My_Cousin_Rachel" title="My Cousin Rachel by Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">My Cousin Rachel</a> and found it to be highly readable and engaging, but in my opinion, it lacks the elegance, intensity and clever structure of <i>Rebecca</i>.<br /><br />After finishing the book, I learned how much of an influence the Brontë sisters had in Du Maurier's writing and, as you read <i>Rachel</i> it's easy to recognize that effect.<br />It's been a few years since I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre" title="Jane Eyre by Charlotte Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Jane Eyre</a> but in many ways, this book reminded me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1036615.Charlotte_Bront_" title="Charlotte Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Charlotte Brontë</a>'s famous gothic tale. Both novels use a first person point of view and share an evocative atmosphere as well as a profound sense of foreboding that permeates throughout the narration.<br /><br />Du Maurier was brilliant at building a feeling of apprehension that gradually envelopes the reader and, by the time you realize it, you are so wrapped in the story that the only way to get out of that "trap" is seeing the book to the end. <br /> <br />Most of the novel revolves around the mystery behind Rachel's motives: Is she the proverbial black widow? Is she truly looking out for the much younger Phillip or exploiting his naiveté? So, villain or not, that is the question. The ambiguity surrounding her character felt at times a little too manipulative, but I appreciate the clues Du Maurier drops, which keeps you invested in the story. Ultimately, the conclusion while not exactly surprising certainly seemed fitting. <br /><br />What kept me from completely getting lost in the narrative was the character of Phillip, which I found rather immature and someone who seemed to be permanently carrying a chip on his shoulder. After Ambrose leaves for Italy, Phillip is somehow capable of managing a large estate and taking on all sorts of responsibilities and yet he behaves like a sophomoric teenager around "his cousin Rachel". His puppy love and overly dramatic attitude would be expected of a 15-year-old, not so much a 25-year-old man. <br /><br />So yes, I am a bit disappointed with this book but I still thought it was a pretty compelling read if for nothing else because I'm still mystified by Rachel. Was she a cold-hearted schemer? An overly ambitious seductress? A product of her upbringing and environment? Just a complex woman with her share of virtues and flaws? All of the above? Du Maurier certainly resists to give us an ending with simplistic answers and moral certitude. Which is why I think this novel remains so fascinating to so many readers: the mystery of Rachel is never quite unraveled.<br /><br />The audiobook, which is beautifully narrated by British actor Jonathan Pryce, gets 5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5494995730910752410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2421140323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2421140323" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17957823-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597778686p2/17957823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2421140323?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/17957823-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781492660637" href="/book/show/34431455-my-cousin-rachel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17957823-erin?shelf=kobo">kobo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2421140323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12744636460463711731"><b> Was Rachel innocent or guilty? Maybe I shall learn that too, in purgatory.</b> <br/><br/>I haven't been reading a lot lately because of exams, report cards, and all those June responsibilities that create tired teachers. Also I recently "discovered " <i> Sense8 </i> on Netflix. But <i>My Cousin Rachel</i> was the kind of book that once opened is <b>impossible to put down.</b> <br/><br/><i> My Cousin Rachel </i> is narrated by 24 year old Philip Ashley. Raised by an older cousin, Ambrose, Philip has lived the lifestyle of the rich and famous. All</span>
  <span id="freeText12744636460463711731" style="display:none"><b> Was Rachel innocent or guilty? Maybe I shall learn that too, in purgatory.</b> <br /><br />I haven't been reading a lot lately because of exams, report cards, and all those June responsibilities that create tired teachers. Also I recently "discovered " <i> Sense8 </i> on Netflix. But <i>My Cousin Rachel</i> was the kind of book that once opened is <b>impossible to put down.</b> <br /><br /><i> My Cousin Rachel </i> is narrated by 24 year old Philip Ashley. Raised by an older cousin, Ambrose, Philip has lived the lifestyle of the rich and famous. All is pretty swell in Philip's world until his cousin takes a vacation in Italy and encounters the widow-Rachel. At first, Philip(oh such a naive youth) believes that Ambrose is just taking pity on a lonely and plain widow. Imagine his shock when he discovers that the couple are soon wed. Then mysterious letters begin to arrive and indicate that Cousin Rachel might not be all that she appears to be. Philip journeys to Italy to discover his cousin dead and the young widow to have fled. <br /><br /><b> I swore that, whatever it had cost Ambrose in pain and suffering before he died, I would return it, in full measure, upon the woman who had caused it....Someday, somehow, I would repay my cousin Rachel. </b><br /><br />So Philip returns to England all bent on revenge and filled with sadness, but everyone around him, including his godfather, caution Philip to not rush to judgement. Soon a letter arrives announcing Rachel's arrival in England and Philip Ashley sets out to discover the truth, but he might just not be able to handle his Cousin Rachel. <br /><br /><b> How simple it must be for a woman of the world, to twist a young man like yourself around her finger.</b> <br /><br />The mounting tension as Rachel and Philip Ashley settle into living under the same roof is pure DuMaurier gold. At times, I forgot that I was holding my breath. I love how she writes her characters in such a way that at times, I hate them and other times I feel empathy for them. <br /><br />So many twists and turns that it will leave your head spin!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1977180037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10187085645724613668">Wow, did Daphne du Maurier ever know how to tell a story! I read "Rebecca" a couple of years ago, more to fill in a gap in my reading history than for any other reason, but it was a riveting gothic suspense novel, and worthy of it's classic status. I bought "My Cousin Rachel" at the same used book sale, and just now got around to it. My word, I think it's even better. It combines a naive and arrogant young man with a worldly "cousin", who had been married to his uncle for a short time, until his</span>
  <span id="freeText10187085645724613668" style="display:none">Wow, did Daphne du Maurier ever know how to tell a story! I read "Rebecca" a couple of years ago, more to fill in a gap in my reading history than for any other reason, but it was a riveting gothic suspense novel, and worthy of it's classic status. I bought "My Cousin Rachel" at the same used book sale, and just now got around to it. My word, I think it's even better. It combines a naive and arrogant young man with a worldly "cousin", who had been married to his uncle for a short time, until his untimely death brings his widow to England. The story builds slowly, with suspicions gathering in the mind of the reader, until (in my case, at least) you are screaming at Phillip on every page, "DON'T BE SO STUPID, OPEN YOUR EYES FOR PETE'S SAKE."<br /><br /> Well, but the ending! Was I, the reader, wrong? Was Phillip wrong? Who was Rachel, really, and what was she thinking? Did my cynicism and suspicion lead me down the wrong path, or was I too quick to jump to judgement? These questions will haunt me for a while.<br /><br />As I said, this woman knew how to tell a story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10187085645724613668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17633854881732640811" style="display:none">“There are some women, Philip, good women very possibly, who through no fault of their own impel disaster. Whatever they touch, somehow turns to tragedy.” <br />― Daphne du Maurier, My Cousin Rachel<br /><br /><br /><br />Did she? didn't she? It's driving me crazy!<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br />I got lost in this book. I just read it recently. I liked it better then Rebecca.<br /><br />I will not list the plot because most people already know. The thing I want to talk about is how amazing the book is. And how I was almost driven crazy by the ending.<br /><br />I had already read this when I suggested it to my book club. I really wanted to see how people reacted to it and what each person's feeling was on the guilt or innocence of Rachel.<br /><br />Most people seemed to feel she did it. I am not so sure. I have no explanation for how the seeds got in her drawer but there was nothing in the letter to suggest she had a hand in anything and the words written to her "if you can't bear to leave him behind" suggest that she too had feelings for Charles. So my take is a bit different then others.<br /><br />I want her to be guilty. It is hard not to start to love Rachel as the book goes on so yes, I'd prefer it if she were a scheming manipulative psycho then the sweet and fun woman she may well have been. I guess we will never know as I read Du Maurier herself did not even have a clear answer on Rachel's guilt.<br /><br />I was surprised it wasn't rated higher on here. I will scroll through some of the reviews as I am curious to see how others felt about Rachel and Phillip. (I could not stand Phillip but I understood, given his sheltered upbringing, how he might have misunderstood certain things.)<br /><br />An excellent book. Now if I just knew the real scoop on the ending..</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2260432805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2260432805" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18894476-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504024458p2/18894476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2260432805?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/18894476-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19007510-my-cousin-rachel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18894476-sarah?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18894476-sarah?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18894476-sarah?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18894476-sarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2260432805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3190813046094635898">I read Daphne Du Maurier's book "Rebecca" and fell in love with it. I read online that "My Cousin Rachel" had a similar feel as "Rebecca". So I decided this was the one to buy. I didn't think it would live up to Rebecca, but I was mistaken. It has the same dark, mysterious atmosphere to it, the same kind of wonderfully developed characters and a great storyline that captivated me from beginning to end. <br/><br/>I read somewhere that the Kindle version which I read, was shorter than the original version. </span>
  <span id="freeText3190813046094635898" style="display:none">I read Daphne Du Maurier's book "Rebecca" and fell in love with it. I read online that "My Cousin Rachel" had a similar feel as "Rebecca". So I decided this was the one to buy. I didn't think it would live up to Rebecca, but I was mistaken. It has the same dark, mysterious atmosphere to it, the same kind of wonderfully developed characters and a great storyline that captivated me from beginning to end. <br /><br />I read somewhere that the Kindle version which I read, was shorter than the original version. I haven't checked that out totally, but now I think I might have to reread at a later date. Not a problem.<br /><br />This emotional novel should most definitely be put in the category of one the greatest classics of all time. It displays the strength of love as a Englishman, Philip, will do anything to get love in return from an Italian woman, Rachel. The reader becomes deep into the story as the plot thickens as a result of the the book's realistic theme. The reader is desperately trying to discover the truth about Rachel until the end when a shocking event occurs. I did enjoy My Cousin Rachel, however, Rebecca is still my favorite of the two. <br /><br />The thing about this book is that once you read it, you will have more questions than when you started!! Is Rachel the sweet, innocent angel she seems to be? Flirty, but naive? Or is she a calculating, evil temptress, who only uses men for her personal gain? And what about Philip? Is he driven mad by jealousy and obsession? Or is there something else at work? The ending is anything but straightforward, and the reader is left to his own to answer these questions. The mystery surrounding Rachel unravels slowly, but in such a way as to keep you on the edge of your seat. <br /><br />This novel is a mix between mystery novel, dark Gothic and gender war, which were woven with clear description and provoking dialogue. Full with paradox and irony but not too full blown. Each character was well drawn: background, personality, way of life (vivid description of Cornwell), and mystery. <br /><br />The ending is superb. I love this authors writings, and the older classics. A lot more than I thought I would. I highly recommend</span>
  <a data-text-id="3190813046094635898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_36056208" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36056208" />
    <a title="Misfit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1375548-misfit"><img alt="Misfit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496595931p2/1375548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36056208?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misfit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misfit" href="/user/show/1375548-misfit">Misfit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781579125691" href="/book/show/50239.My_Cousin_Rachel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36056208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2726721133557731271">Did she or didn’t she? That is the question that will keep readers on the edge of their seat until the final twists on the very last pages. Phillip Ashley was orphaned at a young age and raised in 19C Cornwall by his older cousin Ambrose. Health issues force Ambrose to spend time in warmer climates and he meets and marries a distant cousin Rachel, the widowed Countess Sangaletti. A cryptic note arrives from Ambrose hinting at being poisoned and Phillip heads to Florence to find Ambrose dead of a</span>
  <span id="freeText2726721133557731271" style="display:none">Did she or didn’t she? That is the question that will keep readers on the edge of their seat until the final twists on the very last pages. Phillip Ashley was orphaned at a young age and raised in 19C Cornwall by his older cousin Ambrose. Health issues force Ambrose to spend time in warmer climates and he meets and marries a distant cousin Rachel, the widowed Countess Sangaletti. A cryptic note arrives from Ambrose hinting at being poisoned and Phillip heads to Florence to find Ambrose dead of a brain tumor (so the doctors say.....) and Rachel disappeared, with Rainaldi her close friend and “financial advisor” handling her affairs.<br /><br />Phillip heads home and as rightful heir takes over running the family estate, but constantly broods on his hatred of Rachel and builds an image of her that is completely different when he comes face to face with her. Instead of the murdering she-devil he's built up in his mind, Phillip doesn't quite know what to make of this tiny, elegant and very enigmatic cousin of his. Rachel weaves herself into the lives of Phillip making herself indispensable to the household until Phillip finally finds himself in love with her and forgets his prior suspicions. Phillip realizes his majority at his 25th birthday and he presents Rachel with what Ambrose would have willed to her if he had lived long enough to sign a new will. At that point everything changes between Rachel and Phillip and ………<br /><br />Well I’m not going to tell you, read it for yourself. This was a fabulous read that had me gripped from the very first page and kept me guessing until the very end (actually she still keeps you guessing but you have to read it for yourself to find out why). There’s a good reason Du Maurier is considered the master of romantic suspense. Highly highly recommended. 5/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2726721133557731271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The way du Maurier slowly builds the suspense and mystery was masterful, layer upon layer right up until those final shocking chapters. The characters of the mysterious Rachel and the spoiled an</span>
  <span id="freeText9423944158348053701" style="display:none">"She has done for me at last, Rachel my torment" <br /><br />The question that you will be asking yourself when you finish this book "Did she...or didn't she?" <br /><br />My Cousin Rachel was my first book by Daphne du Maurier and I thought it was brilliant! Written over 75 years ago, this story has such a timeless feel to it. The way du Maurier slowly builds the suspense and mystery was masterful, layer upon layer right up until those final shocking chapters. The characters of the mysterious Rachel and the spoiled and pompous Philip are so cleverly written that you start to question your opinion of them as the story ends. <br /><br />I listened to the audio version of this story and I thought Jonathan Pryce was an excellent narrator. This was my longest audio to date but this story was so captivating I really didn't feel the 11 plus hours of listening time. <br /><br />This book and audio is deserving of 5 huge stars and going right onto my favorites list!<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/29759152-my-cousin-rachel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=strong-female-protagonist">strong-female-protagonist</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2045912044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9238075437898480686">Wow, did Daphne Du Maurier know how to tell a story! This was such a tremendously well-written piece of literature, and I feel pretty disappointed to have finished it. Although, I did buy Jamaica Inn today, so I can continue with my Du Maurier fix. <br/>After reading Rebecca, I just had to buy myself more Du Maurier books. Rebecca completely blew my mind. It was stunning, and I'll probably reread it again in the future. My Cousin Rachel, was a slow burner, everything happened with no sudden haste, an</span>
  <span id="freeText9238075437898480686" style="display:none">Wow, did Daphne Du Maurier know how to tell a story! This was such a tremendously well-written piece of literature, and I feel pretty disappointed to have finished it. Although, I did buy Jamaica Inn today, so I can continue with my Du Maurier fix. <br />After reading Rebecca, I just had to buy myself more Du Maurier books. Rebecca completely blew my mind. It was stunning, and I'll probably reread it again in the future. My Cousin Rachel, was a slow burner, everything happened with no sudden haste, and I was kept guessing, almost until the end. I must say though, it did take me a few chapters to properly immerse myself into the story, but when I did, I couldn't put the book down! When I wasn't reading it, I found myself thinking about it. <br />The gothic atmosphere is something I love in a story, and the scene was set beautifully, for this particular book. As for the characters, their development throughout the story was fantastic, although, I felt like Phillip needed a good shake to enable him to remove his head from the clouds! I'll admit, I made my judgement in regards to Rachel pretty early on, but when I finally finished it, I kind of doubled back on myself. Was Rachel really what I thought she was? Was she just misunderstood? Really, it's haunted me, to be honest, and left my mind reeling, and that, is the key to superb storytelling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9238075437898480686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1554630132" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1554630132" />
    <a title="Dem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2752994-dem"><img alt="Dem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552868566p2/2752994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1554630132?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1554630132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7854682681684378023"><b> 3.5 Stars </b><br/><br/>Having loved Rebecca I wanted to read another novel by Daphne Du Maurier and My Cousin Rachel was next on my list and delighted to say that it doesn't disappoint and has a certain <b>,<i> je ne sais quoi</i></b> about it that had me intrigued.<br/><br/>Written in 1951 this novel is a mystey-romance style novel that is as compelling today as it was back 65 years ago.<br/><br/>Anbrose and Philip run a country estate on the Cornish coast and live a harmonious bachelor lifestyle in an all male household. Ambrose develops </span>
  <span id="freeText7854682681684378023" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 Stars </b><br /><br />Having loved Rebecca I wanted to read another novel by Daphne Du Maurier and My Cousin Rachel was next on my list and delighted to say that it doesn't disappoint and has a certain <b>,<i> je ne sais quoi</i></b> about it that had me intrigued.<br /><br />Written in 1951 this novel is a mystey-romance style novel that is as compelling today as it was back 65 years ago.<br /><br />Anbrose and Philip run a country estate on the Cornish coast and live a harmonious bachelor lifestyle in an all male household. Ambrose develops a few health problems which force him so spend his winters in a warmer climate where he meets and falls in love with "his cousin Rachel" but is Rachel the beautiful delicate angel we are presented with or is there more to Rachel than meets the eye.<br /><br />There is lots of tension in this Gothic style novel and the mystery surrounding Rachel unravels slowly. The writing is vivid and characters well drawn. <br />I loved the fact that du Maurier allows the reader to interact in the story to as you have to read this one carefully and on completing a lot is left up to the readers interpretation.<br /><br />An enjoyable read and I am looking forward to my next novel by Daphne du Maurier.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7854682681684378023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2061627273" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2061627273" />
    <a title="Piyangie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie"><img alt="Piyangie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590579939p2/48056505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2061627273?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piyangie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piyangie" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie">Piyangie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/36462599-my-cousin-rachel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=brittish-lit">brittish-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2061627273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3194421452214654856">This was a fascinating read. Daphne du Maurier has made a name for creating ambiguous stories full of suspense, and <i> My Cousin Rachel</i> does justice to that premise. I have read Rebecca a long time ago and had loved it but for some reason, I have not taken time to explore her other works. And when this book was brought to light by a group read, I felt it was time that I read more of du Maurier. <br/><br/>With her simple and colourful writing du Maurier crafts a beautiful story that talks full of human emoti</span>
  <span id="freeText3194421452214654856" style="display:none">This was a fascinating read. Daphne du Maurier has made a name for creating ambiguous stories full of suspense, and <i> My Cousin Rachel</i> does justice to that premise. I have read Rebecca a long time ago and had loved it but for some reason, I have not taken time to explore her other works. And when this book was brought to light by a group read, I felt it was time that I read more of du Maurier. <br /><br />With her simple and colourful writing du Maurier crafts a beautiful story that talks full of human emotions and human follies. The story is half told and is left open-ended. But Du Maurier has laid the facts beautifully allowing the readers to draw their own conclusion. Although it taxes one, I liked du Maurier’s style of keeping the story ambiguous. <br /><br />I have always told myself not to have first impressions upon the characters, but too often I forget this resolution. So when Rachel was introduced, I saw her with a guilty eye. From that point of view, it was easy to dislike her. Then there were the characters of Ambrose and Philip. The former is a victim, but of nature or human misconduct is difficult to discern. While some accept the former cause as the reason for his death, Philip sticks to the latter relying on certain letters he received from Ambrose. And half though the book I agreed with Philip. Philip is a naïve and innocent young man with poor knowledge of the world and especially of women. He was raised by a man who himself was reserved from the female society. He was a “boy” for his age and was stupid beyond measures. His infatuation with Rachel makes him forget his initial suspicion of the woman and this same infatuation allows Rachel to manipulate Philip to her own advantage. Although I liked and sympathized with Philip initially, soon this feeling changed and replaced with annoyance. His stupid thinking and conduct were beyond my comprehension. With this perspective, I reached the end of the story only to be greeted by an uncomfortable feeling that I was fooled. Was Philip naive and stupid as I thought? Was Rachel guilty? Of greed, I was sure but of murder? Was Rachel the villain or was it, Philip? A whole set of unanswered questions started nagging at me.<br /><br />The supporting characters were quite interesting. I liked them, perhaps more so than the main characters. They provided a colourful backdrop to the story and greater contrast to the main characters. <br /><br />Overall, it was a very enjoyable read and a good beginning for my returning to du Maurier. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3194421452214654856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1920228209823411894"><b>4.5/5.</b> This was definitely a highlight of my reading year so far! It's a rather slow, but quietly unsettling story of distrust, obsession and ambiguity. Most of the story is set on a large country estate on the Cornish coast and I loved the descriptions of the landscape and atmosphere. Plus, the way du Maurier manages to play with and twist the reader's loyalties is absolutely incredible. Highly recommend this one!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9121948882270484792">I don’t... <br/><br/>Ok so I recently read (and loved) Rebecca by Daphne du Maurier & so imagine my excitement to read another gothic romance/thriller she wrote. I had such high hopes for this, especially given the number of people who I’ve seen consider this somehow <b>better</b> than Rebecca. <br/><br/>I’ll be honest here. 1 Star, that’s kind of an extreme rating. But giving it a 2 Stars or even a 1.5 Stars just doesn’t feel like it genuinely represents how bad of a time I had while reading this. I’m struggling to find </span>
  <span id="freeText9121948882270484792" style="display:none">I don’t... <br /><br />Ok so I recently read (and loved) Rebecca by Daphne du Maurier &amp; so imagine my excitement to read another gothic romance/thriller she wrote. I had such high hopes for this, especially given the number of people who I’ve seen consider this somehow <b>better</b> than Rebecca. <br /><br />I’ll be honest here. 1 Star, that’s kind of an extreme rating. But giving it a 2 Stars or even a 1.5 Stars just doesn’t feel like it genuinely represents how bad of a time I had while reading this. I’m struggling to find even one thing I liked about this???<br /><br />Plot? <b>Boring.</b> <br />Atmosphere? <b>Boring.</b> <br />Characters? <b>Double Dog Boring.</b><br />Conclusion?? <b>BORING &amp; PREDICTABLE &amp; DID I MENTION BORING?</b> which honestly just put the shit cherry on top of this shit sundae. <br /><br />Seriously I felt like I was just <i>waiting &amp; waiting</i> for something even the <b>slightest bit interesting</b> to take place but I was disappointed right up to the very end. <br /><br />I couldn’t bring myself to care about any of these characters but I especially did not give a rat’s ass about Philip Ashley. <b>Wow what a dumb fuck?</b><br /><br />I know like “young &amp; stupid love” and “infatuation to the point of lunacy” are definitely themes here but watching Philip was like watching a kid break its own toy &amp; then throw a crazy ass fit when realizing the toy is broken. <br /><br />Alright I’m kidding there was one thing about this novel that wasn’t absolute garbage: the writing style! Of course Daphne du Maurier is wonderful at gothic English mansions &amp; posh English dialogue. But even being written nicely wasn’t enough to keep me from groaning.<br /><br />All the while I kept thinking that reading this novel felt like a reading assignment from high school that I was forced to slog through &amp; pretend to like &amp; pull some convoluted meanings out of my ass about. And you know what? A book that makes me feel that gross deserves a 1 Star. <br /><br />If you’re struggling between Rebecca &amp; My Cousin Rachel to begin your journey into Daphne du Maurier‘s work? It’s gonna be a Rebecca from me, folks.</span>

<div id="review_143681890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143681890" />
    <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again"><img alt="Jeanette (Again)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304653755p2/796425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143681890?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette (Again)" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again">Jeanette (Again)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781844080403" href="/book/show/162543.My_Cousin_Rachel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=europe-and-british-isles">europe-and-british-isles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=four-star-fiction">four-star-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=all-fiction">all-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=miss-trees">miss-trees</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143681890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12907072117825396275">There <i>is</i> a mystery at the heart of this story, but it's mostly about unrequited puppy love in the extreme. I spent almost the entire book thinking <i>don't do it, Philip, don't do it!</i>, but he's a lovesick fool, and hardheaded to boot. I felt so sorry for Louise Kendall throughout the story. She's such a dear girl and loyal friend, and too decent to butt in when she ought to. I don't really know how to feel about Rachel. If I had a younger man gaga over me like that, I can't say I wouldn't take adva</span>
  <span id="freeText12907072117825396275" style="display:none">There <i>is</i> a mystery at the heart of this story, but it's mostly about unrequited puppy love in the extreme. I spent almost the entire book thinking <i>don't do it, Philip, don't do it!</i>, but he's a lovesick fool, and hardheaded to boot. I felt so sorry for Louise Kendall throughout the story. She's such a dear girl and loyal friend, and too decent to butt in when she ought to. I don't really know how to feel about Rachel. If I had a younger man gaga over me like that, I can't say I wouldn't take advantage of it in some way, although I'd be a lot more honest and open.<br /> Dame Daphne is the tease of all teases, stringing you along throughout an entire book thinking things are one way, then zapping you at the end with a big twist that places the entire story in a new light. She does the same thing in <i>Rebecca</i>, which I think is the better of the two books because it has a more sinister edge. If you care to delve a little deeper, you'll see that both stories are also about lack of communication and the assumptions made simply because people fail to ask the right questions or speak forthrightly. <br /><br />I know this isn't much of a review with regard to plot or characters, but I'm hesitant to review du Maurier for fear of giving something away that will steal something from another reader's enjoyment. Every little detail I discovered along the way was something I was glad no one had shared with me ahead of time. If you love old-fashioned storytelling and you're a reasonably patient reader, you'll enjoy <i>My Cousin Rachel</i> for all the lovely little details and skillful mind manipulation. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12907072117825396275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_236048229" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236048229" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542979-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454402751p2/4542979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236048229?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781844080403" href="/book/show/162543.My_Cousin_Rachel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=buddy-reads-with-jemidar">buddy-reads-with-jemidar</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236048229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3520166295296457881"><br/>To think that just a few short months ago, I was under the impression that Daphne du Maurier only wrote one novel worth reading, the splendid <i>Rebecca</i>. I could not have been more wrong. <br/><br/><i>My Cousin Rachel</i> is a wonderful read. A psychological thriller, the novel is set in 19th Century Cornwall and in Florence. The narrator, Philip Ashley, falls in love with – or rather, becomes obsessed with - his cousin’s widow, Rachel, who may or may not be a murderess. The development and consequences of Philip’s</span>
  <span id="freeText3520166295296457881" style="display:none"><br />To think that just a few short months ago, I was under the impression that Daphne du Maurier only wrote one novel worth reading, the splendid <i>Rebecca</i>. I could not have been more wrong. <br /><br /><i>My Cousin Rachel</i> is a wonderful read. A psychological thriller, the novel is set in 19th Century Cornwall and in Florence. The narrator, Philip Ashley, falls in love with – or rather, becomes obsessed with - his cousin’s widow, Rachel, who may or may not be a murderess. The development and consequences of Philip’s obsession are at the heart of the novel. <br /><br />There is so much to admire about this work. Firstly, there is the beautiful descriptive language in which Maurier evokes the natural beauty of Cornwall and the drama of Florence. Secondly, there is the superb use of a male first person narrator, who reveals things to the reader of which he is himself unaware. Thirdly, there is the fascinating ambiguity of the characters and the narrative. While Rachel’s character and actions are open to question and interpretation, so is Philip’s reliability as a narrator. <br /><br />Overall, this is a gem of novel. It is easy to read and hard to put down, a totally engaging page-turner which gives readers plenty to ponder at the end. Contemporary thriller writers could learn a thing or two from Daphne du Maurier. Another enjoyable buddy read with my friend Jemidar. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3520166295296457881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5xuUaxl1ymy2zyV80bV6KyZiveATlPOOvqVF+PpvXJVZCitC/GrOHDcsC6XpN3XLq5e+NiGvJ+RCo78QaJva1w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ItS83z9fQpTy4y7KfJNseIcevWL8iXIycOQVoccJHQ+cxQP22kBG5HMAABNEEWOYCuu+tM6ypliM4u9JVf2bTQ==')})
  }

From the author of Gods of Jade and Shadow comes “a terrifying twist on classic gothic horror” (Kirkus Reviews) set in glamorous 1950s Mexico.\n \nAfter receiving a frantic letter from her newlywed cousin begging for someone to save her from a mysterious doom, Noemí Taboada heads to High Place, a distant house in the Mexican countryside. She’s not sure what she will find - her cousin’s husband, a handsome Englishman, is a stranger, and Noemí knows little about the region. \n\nNoemí is also an unlikely rescuer: She’s a glamorous debutante, and her chic gowns and perfect red lipstick are more suited for cocktail parties than amateur sleuthing. But she’s also tough and smart, with an indomitable will, and she is not afraid: not of her cousin’s new husband, who is both menacing and alluring; not of his father, the ancient patriarch who seems to be fascinated by Noemí; and not even of the house itself, which begins to invade Noemi’s dreams with visions of blood and doom. \n\nHer only ally in this inhospitable abode is the family’s youngest son. Shy and gentle, he seems to want to help Noemí but might also be hiding dark knowledge of his family’s past. For there are many secrets behind the walls of High Place. The family’s once colossal wealth and faded mining empire kept them from prying eyes, but as Noemí digs deeper she unearths stories of violence and madness. \n\nAnd Noemí, mesmerized by the terrifying       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2001717.Daphne_du_Maurier">About Daphne du Maurier</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2001717.Daphne_du_Maurier"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1422444467p3/2001717.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2001717.Daphne_du_Maurier">Daphne du Maurier
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
6,202
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10199309733859489575">If Daphne du Maurier had written only <i>Rebecca</i>, she would still be one of the great shapers of popular culture and the modern imagination. Few writers have created more magical and mysterious places than Jamaica Inn and Manderley, buildings invested with a rich character that gives them a memorable life of their own.<br/><br/>In many ways the life of Daphne du Maurier resembles a fairy tale. Born into a fami</span>
  <span id="freeText10199309733859489575" style="display:none">If Daphne du Maurier had written only <i>Rebecca</i>, she would still be one of the great shapers of popular culture and the modern imagination. Few writers have created more magical and mysterious places than Jamaica Inn and Manderley, buildings invested with a rich character that gives them a memorable life of their own.<br /><br />In many ways the life of Daphne du Maurier resembles a fairy tale. Born into a family with a rich artistic and historical background, the daughter of a famous actor-manager, she was indulged as a child and grew up enjoying enormous freedom from financial and parental restraint. She spent her youth sailing boats, travelling on the Continent with friends, and writing stories. A prestigious publishing house accepted her first novel when she was in her early twenties, and its publication brought her not only fame but the attentions of a handsome soldier, Major (later Lieutenant-General Sir) Frederick Browning, whom she married.<br /><br />Her subsequent novels became bestsellers, earning her enormous wealth and fame. While Alfred Hitchcock's film based upon her novel proceeded to make her one of the best-known authors in the world, she enjoyed the life of a fairy princess in a mansion in Cornwall called Menabilly, which served as the model for Manderley in <i>Rebecca</i>.<br /><br />Daphne du Maurier was obsessed with the past. She intensively researched the lives of Francis and Anthony Bacon, the history of Cornwall, the Regency period, and nineteenth-century France and England. Above all, however, she was obsessed with her own family history, which she chronicled in <i>Gerald: A Portrait</i>, a biography of her father; <i>The du Mauriers</i>, a study of her family which focused on her grandfather, George du Maurier, the novelist and illustrator for Punch; <i>The Glassblowers</i>, a novel based upon the lives of her du Maurier ancestors; and <i>Growing Pains</i>, an autobiography that ignores nearly 50 years of her life in favour of the joyful and more romantic period of her youth. Daphne du Maurier can best be understood in terms of her remarkable and paradoxical family, the ghosts which haunted her life and fiction.<br /><br />While contemporary writers were dealing critically with such subjects as the war, alienation, religion, poverty, Marxism, psychology and art, and experimenting with new techniques such as the stream of consciousness, du Maurier produced 'old-fashioned' novels with straightforward narratives that appealed to a popular audience's love of fantasy, adventure, sexuality and mystery. At an early age, she recognised that her readership was comprised principally of women, and she cultivated their loyal following through several decades by embodying their desires and dreams in her novels and short stories.<br /><br />In some of her novels, however, she went beyond the technique of the formulaic romance to achieve a powerful psychological realism reflecting her intense feelings about her father, and to a lesser degree, her mother. This vision, which underlies <i>Julius</i>, <i>Rebecca</i> and <i>The Parasites</i>, is that of an author overwhelmed by the memory of her father's commanding presence. In <i>Julius</i> and <i>The Parasites</i>, for example, she introduces the image of a domineering but deadly father and the daring subject of incest.<br /><br />In <i>Rebecca</i>, on the other hand, du Maurier fuses psychological realism with a sophisticated version of the Cinderella story. The nameless heroine has been saved from a life of drudgery by marrying a handsome, wealthy aristocrat, but unlike the Prince in Cinderella, Maxim de Winter is old enough to be the narrator's father. The narrator thus must do battle with The Other Woman—the dead Rebecca and her witch-like surrogate, Mrs Danvers—to win the love of her husband and father-figure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10199309733859489575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
